  <a href="#other_reviews" class="actionLinkLite votes">
      <span itemprop="ratingCount" title="2010" class="value-title">2,010 Ratings</span>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5252588362095778190"><em>Tapping the Dream Tree</em> collects 18 stories by bestselling contemporary fantasy master Charles de Lint. One story, "The Witching Hour," is original to this volume, with a few others taken from limited-edition chapbooks; the remaining tales have been drawn from an impressive diversity of magazines and anthologies. The stories are set in and around de Lint's mythic, haunted A</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5252588362095778190"><em>Tapping the Dream Tree</em> collects 18 stories by bestselling contemporary fantasy master Charles de Lint. One story, "The Witching Hour," is original to this volume, with a few others taken from limited-edition chapbooks; the remaining tales have been drawn from an impressive diversity of magazines and anthologies. The stories are set in and around de Lint's mythic, haunted American city of Newford, and fans will recognize several characters from de Lint's popular series.<p>The powerful story "Ten for The Devil" is a superb choice for an opener: it showcases de Lint's literary strengths and treats of his recurring themes of magic, music, creativity, and human worth. Musician Staley Cross's grandmother has always warned her to be careful when she plays her blue fiddle. But Staley never quite believed that her music could rouse dangerous magic... until one night, playing in a faraway field, she discovers the Devil doesn't only go down to Georgia. First published before the filming of <em>O Brother, Where Art Thou?</em>, "Ten for the Devil" draws upon the same crossroads myth as does the movie, but takes a very different road as it follows Staley's search for her only hope of soul survival: a mysterious bluesman known as Robert. <em>--Cynthia Ward</em><br /><br />"The [Newford] books have all been written in such a way that you should be able to pick up any one and get a full and complete story. However, characters do reoccur, off center stage as it were, and their stories do follow a sequence."</p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5252588362095778190">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_30673375">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30673375" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1303301-julia" class="left imgcol" title="Julia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1240083650p2/1303301.jpg" alt="Julia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/30673375?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1303301-julia" class="user" title="Julia">Julia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/186440.Tapping_the_Dream_Tree" title="Softcover 9780312868406" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1303301-julia?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1303301-julia?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer30673375">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7484229851861427389">What a <em>great</em> collection! Rereading “Trading Hearts at the Half Kaffe Cafe” got me thinking that Adrian Paul (the actor who did "Highlander" the tv show) would be <em>perfect</em> as Lyle the shy investment counselor/ werewolf and I never do that. <br />“Making a Noise in This World” reminded me of something <a title="Sherman Alexie" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4174.Sherman_Alexie">Sherman Alexie</a> would write and maybe film. <br />“Embracing the Mystery” and “Pixel Pixies” are both about the used bookseller Holly Rue. “The Witching Hour” is about Geordie and Christie’s brother who only did t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7484229851861427389">What a <em>great</em> collection! Rereading “Trading Hearts at the Half Kaffe Cafe” got me thinking that Adrian Paul (the actor who did "Highlander" the tv show) would be <em>perfect</em> as Lyle the shy investment counselor/ werewolf and I never do that. <br />“Making a Noise in This World” reminded me of something <a title="Sherman Alexie" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4174.Sherman_Alexie">Sherman Alexie</a> would write and maybe film. <br />“Embracing the Mystery” and “Pixel Pixies” are both about the used bookseller Holly Rue. “The Witching Hour” is about Geordie and Christie’s brother who only did the right thing at the very end of his life. <br />“Seven Wild Sisters” is a wonderful 144 page novella set in the same universe as de Lint’s story about a West Virginia mountain girl who finds a painting box. In “Seven Wild Sisters” she’s an old woman with another teenager learning from her. I could only wish that Sarah Jane finished high school. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7484229851861427389">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/6762949-arielle-walker" class="left imgcol" title="Arielle Walker"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1403749241p2/6762949.jpg" alt="Arielle Walker" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/619596715?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6762949-arielle-walker" class="user" title="Arielle Walker">Arielle Walker</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6762949-arielle-walker?shelf=fantasy-unusual" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-unusual</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6762949-arielle-walker?shelf=short-stories-and-novellas" class="actionLinkLite">short-stories-and-novellas</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer619596715">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3135080676595835646">And again, de Lint makes his way back to my "favourite authors" list. While not quite reaching the magic of Dreams Underfoot, Tapping the Dream Tree is filled with beautiful writing and this time, most of the stories are heart-warming too. There are only two here that I would consider dark, involving an innocent boy on death row, and also a ghost seeking revenge on a serial killer. <br /><br />The other stories are fanciful and lovely (though often still with that hint of darkness). There's the werewolf goi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3135080676595835646">And again, de Lint makes his way back to my "favourite authors" list. While not quite reaching the magic of Dreams Underfoot, Tapping the Dream Tree is filled with beautiful writing and this time, most of the stories are heart-warming too. There are only two here that I would consider dark, involving an innocent boy on death row, and also a ghost seeking revenge on a serial killer. <br /><br />The other stories are fanciful and lovely (though often still with that hint of darkness). There's the werewolf going on a blind date after putting an ad in the paper; the hob who organises the books in a second-hand book-store; Sophie returning to the dreamworld for yet another adventure and, of course, Jilly Coppercorn. <br /><br />If this sounds at all "childish", I assure you it is not, though all his writing - yes, even the darkest - retains that sense of childhood wonder that I think the majority of us have lost. </span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer273668784">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12311187631051273876">what i love about Charles de Lint's books are (1) how the world is recognizably ours but with magic just sort of off to the side where you're not looking; (2) how people are generally good -- not perfect, sometimes total screwups, but always having a decent core; (3) how it inspires you to appreciate your own life, whatever it is, without being all preachy about it. <br /><br />I'm pretty sure this could be a decent intro to the Newford series -- it definitely helps to have met some of the characters before</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12311187631051273876">what i love about Charles de Lint's books are (1) how the world is recognizably ours but with magic just sort of off to the side where you're not looking; (2) how people are generally good -- not perfect, sometimes total screwups, but always having a decent core; (3) how it inspires you to appreciate your own life, whatever it is, without being all preachy about it. <br /><br />I'm pretty sure this could be a decent intro to the Newford series -- it definitely helps to have met some of the characters before, but wouldn't be necessary i don't think.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/5866692-mel" class="user" title="Mel">Mel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5866692-mel?shelf=21st-century-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">21st-century-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1032539386">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5033754929741010455">De Lint has spent a lot of time looking at the blending of native American myths and European myths in his stories. This collection included some Christian mythology too, which was interesting. I found it harder to get into this collection, though I'm not sure I blame this so much on De Lint but rather on the people I've known who believe in fairies and spirits and part of the living in the modern world and having that part be real just reminded me a little too much of them. <br /><br />But there were some</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5033754929741010455">De Lint has spent a lot of time looking at the blending of native American myths and European myths in his stories. This collection included some Christian mythology too, which was interesting. I found it harder to get into this collection, though I'm not sure I blame this so much on De Lint but rather on the people I've known who believe in fairies and spirits and part of the living in the modern world and having that part be real just reminded me a little too much of them. <br /><br />But there were some nice stories that seemed like fairy tales, there were some interesting new ideas about ghosts, I think my favorite was about a man who sold his soul to the "devil" only to have the devil turn out to be a benevolent soul who was only interested in helping people improve themselves. But over all I did find it a little disappointing, but I think that might be my fault and not the authors. But it all seemed a little too simplistic and well meaning at times.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_807940214">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/807940214" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15605769-steve-bouchard" class="left imgcol" title="Steve Bouchard"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1357098658p2/15605769.jpg" alt="Steve Bouchard" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/807940214?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 01, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15605769-steve-bouchard" class="user" title="Steve Bouchard">Steve Bouchard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/186440.Tapping_the_Dream_Tree" title="Softcover 9780312868406" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer807940214">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5568234506771498579">I love Charles de Lint's books, even though I haven't been keeping up with them for the past several years. "Yarrow" was one of the first fanasy books I read, and he quickly became a favorite author. It's his dependable mix of myth into real life that's a constant draw. That said, this is a typical Newford collection. Not that it's a bad thing, but the cut of story is usually pretty similar--slices of life where reality and magic meet; people coming to terms with who they are and what's (previou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5568234506771498579">I love Charles de Lint's books, even though I haven't been keeping up with them for the past several years. "Yarrow" was one of the first fanasy books I read, and he quickly became a favorite author. It's his dependable mix of myth into real life that's a constant draw. That said, this is a typical Newford collection. Not that it's a bad thing, but the cut of story is usually pretty similar--slices of life where reality and magic meet; people coming to terms with who they are and what's (previously) unseen around them.<br /><br />So for me there were not very many surpirses here, but a lot of good bedtime reading all the same. There are a few stories that stretch the comfortable norm of a de Lint story, like "The Witching Hour" and "Freak." Although it's not entirely out of character if you've read his horror books under Samuel M. Key.<br /><br />The best story, for me, was the endpiece novella, "Seven Wild Sisters." It's typical fare, but delivered at a refreshing fast pace. Centered around the age-old war between the 'sangmen (ginseng) and bee people, I couldn't help but be reminded of Alice in Wonderland (ie Bee Queen as the Queen of Hearts), and it was cool seeing de Lint subtly pull in aspects from a classic piece that sits outside of the classic fare he usually draws from.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5568234506771498579">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/463971156?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1173726-k-axel" class="user" title="K. Axel">K. Axel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/186440.Tapping_the_Dream_Tree" title="Softcover 9780312868406" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1173726-k-axel?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1173726-k-axel?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer463971156">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10891320854647208120">I've always loved Charles de Lint since I read a story by him, about a man and the tree from his childhood. I don't remember all the details, as you can clearly tell (its been maybe... 10-13 years since I read it), but I remember the feeling that I had when I read the story and it was a warm feeling, but also that this story was somehow directly connected to me and my life (I had a tree much like that in my backyard).<br /><br />Anyways, years later I pick up this collection on a whim and drops it off at th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10891320854647208120">I've always loved Charles de Lint since I read a story by him, about a man and the tree from his childhood. I don't remember all the details, as you can clearly tell (its been maybe... 10-13 years since I read it), but I remember the feeling that I had when I read the story and it was a warm feeling, but also that this story was somehow directly connected to me and my life (I had a tree much like that in my backyard).<br /><br />Anyways, years later I pick up this collection on a whim and drops it off at the Shelf of Lost Stories. I want to read it, but I also want to read about... 546 other books. However, maybe a year later, I start to read the first story, but it becomes clear to me that I am definitely not ready for the book yet, and so I put it back on its place on the Shelf.<br /><br />But four days ago, I finally spot the book again and have this incredible feeling that I am ready to delve into its secret and lo and behold... I was, and... am.<br /><br />Since this is a collection of shortstories, this will be another review-in-progress where I will write a short review of each story as I read them. As has become the norm of late... I will start at the very beginning.<br /><br /><strong>Ten for the Devil</strong> (45 pages)<br />Staley is a young woman who lives in the rez, in a trailer, and who loves to play her very special blue fiddle. One day she is dropped off not far from her home and when she plays her fiddle on a whim, she accidently summons something from the otherworld. She brings a rabbit, a skinchanger, with her to her friends, all in the hopes that they can tell her what is going on. Great story with a lot of mysterious insight into the world that we live in. The ending left a little to be desired, as it ended rather quickly, however, this story still comes highly recommended. (4 stars)<br /><br /><strong>Wingless Angels</strong> (17 pages)<br />A man finds a camera one day, with strange pictures dated a week later. Not only that, it also appears that the strange creatures on the picture is killing a man. Is the guy losing his mind, or is this another weird occurence in the town of Newford? This wont ever be my favorite Newford story as it lacks the beauty of other Newford stories, but... I might have to go back to it one day. (2 stars)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10891320854647208120">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_700054650">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/700054650" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1608798-bethany" class="left imgcol" title="Bethany"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1443144239p2/1608798.jpg" alt="Bethany" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/700054650?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1608798-bethany" class="user" title="Bethany">Bethany</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/186440.Tapping_the_Dream_Tree" title="Softcover 9780312868406" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fantasy and short story readers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=myths-and-legends" class="actionLinkLite">myths-and-legends</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=short-stories" class="actionLinkLite">short-stories</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=other-world" class="actionLinkLite">other-world</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=out-of-the-box-thinking" class="actionLinkLite">out-of-the-box-thinking</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=rated-pg-13" class="actionLinkLite">rated-pg-13</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=rated-r" class="actionLinkLite">rated-r</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1608798-bethany?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer700054650">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer658617624287207961">This is a collection of short stories about Newford, a town that Charles de Lint really likes writing about. In Newford, everything has a magical twist to it, and there are doorways to other worlds and mythological creatures walking the streets. <br /><br /><strong>The Good:</strong><br /><br />The stories in themselves were interesting, and I have been finding myself more and more attracted to short story books. I am an English major, and in the last few months, I have become fascinated by the way that authors can use a few pages to c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText658617624287207961">This is a collection of short stories about Newford, a town that Charles de Lint really likes writing about. In Newford, everything has a magical twist to it, and there are doorways to other worlds and mythological creatures walking the streets. <br /><br /><strong>The Good:</strong><br /><br />The stories in themselves were interesting, and I have been finding myself more and more attracted to short story books. I am an English major, and in the last few months, I have become fascinated by the way that authors can use a few pages to create entire worlds and complex characters with histories and backgrounds and relationships. <br /><br />I also liked the way that music was the connecting link between the stories. In this book, music = magic (or is at least a doorway to another world). I love that idea, particularly since de Lint picks up on the fact that music is a nonverbal language in and of itself, and he uses that to appeal to his readers. <br /><br />I have to say that my favorite of all the stories was also the longest. "Seven Wild Sisters" is the most complex, lengthy, and well-drawn story, as well as the most magical for me. Oh, and by that point in the book, Charles de Lint figured out how to use POV cues. (Refer to rant below.)<br /><br /><strong>The Bad:</strong> <br /><br />The POV drove me <em>crazy</em>. Really, short stories don't need a constant change of viewpoint, and if Charles de Lint had followed the golden rule of writing (write about what you know), that would have helped the book, too! There were a couple of different aspects of the POV that consistently bothered me.<br /><br />First of all, Charles de Lint often writes from a woman's perspective in the first person, and he can't always pull it off. I would say that at least half of the stories are written [mostly] from a woman's perspective, but for many of those, I had to directly read the overt character identifying statements given <em>by other characters</em> to realize this. I usually thought that the narrator was a teenage or adult guy, but was sometimes shocked later on to find that the narrator was, in fact, a girl or woman. Charles de Lint honestly has a masculine writing style, and that is not bad. I think that he needs to capitulate on that more. Actually, on second thought, that statement needs to be modified. I think that he shouldn't write so often from a girl/woman's perspective, but when he writes from a man's POV, he doesn't need to get into gross stuff either. The paragraph about masturbation in <em>Freak</em> made me positively ill, and I thought that it was entirely unnecessary. <br /><br />Second of all, the POV constantly changed. Charles de Lint would go from 3rd person to 1st person to another 1st person narration and repeat the process randomly. I was frequently confused as to whom was speaking, if anyone. This confusion was exacerbated by the fact that there were only two stories with POV-changes that had cues. I absolutely depend on such clues to discern differences between narrators most of the time. It was truly disorienting to read one paragraph in a 1st-person voice and then to go to the next paragraph to find that...someone else is narrating about the narrator in the first paragraph. That just breaks up the flow of the story. <br /><br />Aside from the POV problems, I have not been happy with Charles de Lint's use of profanity. For me, less [profanity] is more [reader happiness]. Fortunately, the profanity level was much less than in <em>Dingo</em>, but it was still occasionally present, and I winced every time a swear word appeared. In fact, swearing often seemed to be grouped according to story. Some stories had none at all, whereas some had profane narrators. I don't think that profanity should really be a character-builder.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="658617624287207961">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/140245483?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 12, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3726509-lis-carey" class="user" title="Lis Carey">Lis Carey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3726509-lis-carey?shelf=f-sf" class="actionLinkLite">f-sf</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer140245483">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15533635653628122483">This is a hefty collection of de Lint's Newford short stories, several of them published previously available only in limited edition chapbooks or collections, and one of them, "The Witching Hour," is original to this collection. There's a good mix here of the optimistic and the grim, familiar Newford characters and new faces. Jilly, Geordie, and Christy each have the lead in stories of their own, while others feature new characters or characters who have been minor figures in other Newford tale</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15533635653628122483">This is a hefty collection of de Lint's Newford short stories, several of them published previously available only in limited edition chapbooks or collections, and one of them, "The Witching Hour," is original to this collection. There's a good mix here of the optimistic and the grim, familiar Newford characters and new faces. Jilly, Geordie, and Christy each have the lead in stories of their own, while others feature new characters or characters who have been minor figures in other Newford tales. There's some variety in the settings, as well, with Christy's story taking place during a book tour, and others set more in the hills around Newford than in the city itself.<br /><br />"Freak" and "The Witching Hour" are undeniably grim in tone, while "Big City Littles" is completely charming, and "Seven Wild Sisters," my favorite of the collection, is a satisfying, adventurous modern fairy tale. Other stories in the collection strik e a wide range of moods and tones, and the overall quality is high. This is enjoable reading for a Newford fan, and probably a good introduction for someone not familiar with de Lint's work.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15533635653628122483">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer304267831">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12357547619680803724">After a couple of grim novels in a row, followed by a nonfiction, I needed something like Charles de Lint’s fantasy to clear my mental palate. This thick volume of short stories (all but one being reprints) did the job. These are Newford stories, my favorite fantasy place. <br /><br />Newford is a special place. It’s a fairly big city, somewhere in North America, with brand new parts and old, run down parts. There are a lot of artistic folks living there, and the city shares its space with magical, non-huma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12357547619680803724">After a couple of grim novels in a row, followed by a nonfiction, I needed something like Charles de Lint’s fantasy to clear my mental palate. This thick volume of short stories (all but one being reprints) did the job. These are Newford stories, my favorite fantasy place. <br /><br />Newford is a special place. It’s a fairly big city, somewhere in North America, with brand new parts and old, run down parts. There are a lot of artistic folks living there, and the city shares its space with magical, non-human people, too. There are faeries and hobs and witches, and these European magical beings rub elbows old spirits of the First Nations. The barrier between worlds is thin in Newford, it seems. <br /><br />Like any anthology, the material varies in quality. Some are brilliant stories with fully realized characters, while some are slight. A few, like ‘Wingless Angels’ and ‘Many Worlds are Born Tonight’ are unusually dark for de Lint- fantasy noir, the grim side that all places have. <br /><br />I had read over half of the stories in this book before (including the novella ‘Seven Wild Sisters’, which was originally published as a standalone novel), but I enjoyed revisiting the ones I read as much as discovering the ones unfamiliar to me. <br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_244707981">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244707981" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7038421-isabel-kittiwake" class="left imgcol" title="Isabel (kittiwake)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1322770851p2/7038421.jpg" alt="Isabel (kittiwake)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/244707981?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 08, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7038421-isabel-kittiwake" class="user" title="Isabel (kittiwake)">Isabel (kittiwake)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/186440.Tapping_the_Dream_Tree" title="Softcover 9780312868406" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer244707981">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17067312450191638674"><em>"I lived in a tree," he said. "Not in some little house nestled up in its branches, but deep inside the trunk itself where the sap flows and old secrets cluster. It was a time, let me tell you, but long gone now. Then I was a king in a forest of green, now I live like a beggar in a forest of stone."</em><br /><br />Lots of short stories plus a novella called "Seven Wild Sisters".<br /><br />Unfortunately, this book contains <strong> <em>the most annoying</em> </strong> story called "The Words that Remain". A young woman who is brilliant at every cre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17067312450191638674"><em>"I lived in a tree," he said. "Not in some little house nestled up in its branches, but deep inside the trunk itself where the sap flows and old secrets cluster. It was a time, let me tell you, but long gone now. Then I was a king in a forest of green, now I live like a beggar in a forest of stone."</em><br /><br />Lots of short stories plus a novella called "Seven Wild Sisters".<br /><br />Unfortunately, this book contains <strong>
  <em>the most annoying</em>
</strong> story called "The Words that Remain". A young woman who is brilliant at every creative activity she has tried and could have been a professional, singer, artist, musician, or whatever else she turned her hand to, is persuaded by her father to follow him into the hotel business. Instead of finding fulfilment in having creative hobbies, she kills off her creative side so thoroughly that it becomes a ghost haunting the hotel she works in! The protagonists of Charles de Lint's stories are nearly always artists or musicians, either professionals or else working at some dead-end job while following their artistic vocation and trying to make it professionally. He seems to despise anyone in a normal job, and think that they must have no interior life, imagination or spark of creativity. In his mind, if you aren't a professional creative you might as well despair of your life and go and live on the streets, because no-one else counts! It's a pity really, because I do like Charles de Lint's magical and life-affirming stories except for certain niggling irritations, and his books are all staying in my bookcase for a future re-read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17067312450191638674">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a href="/review/show/64695388?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 18, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1874367-kerry" class="user" title="Kerry">Kerry</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1874367-kerry?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1874367-kerry?shelf=everything" class="actionLinkLite">everything</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer64695388">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14089052275064567610">As much as I enjoy the full lenght novels in Charles de Lint's Newford series, I have to say that I think I enjoy his short story anthologies even more. This one, Tapping the Dream Tree, had a wide range of stories. From the fairly light-hearted Pixel Pixies, Big City Littles and Trading Hearts at the Half Kaffe Cafe to the darker (and freakier) <br />Wingless Angels and Sign Here, there is a little something for every taste. <br /><br />My particular favorite story was The Words that Remain, where a woman litera</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14089052275064567610">As much as I enjoy the full lenght novels in Charles de Lint's Newford series, I have to say that I think I enjoy his short story anthologies even more. This one, Tapping the Dream Tree, had a wide range of stories. From the fairly light-hearted Pixel Pixies, Big City Littles and Trading Hearts at the Half Kaffe Cafe to the darker (and freakier) <br />Wingless Angels and Sign Here, there is a little something for every taste. <br /><br />My particular favorite story was The Words that Remain, where a woman literally casts off the part of her nature that was free spirited and creative to focus on the mundane reality of running her family's hotel only to have that free spirt become a ghost of the person she was. <br /><br />I also enjoyed revisiting with some of my favorite Newford characters, especially in the Buffalo Man which features several of my favorites: (the Kelledy's, the Crow Girls and Jilly) all together. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14089052275064567610">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/22180864-johanna-haas" class="user" title="Johanna Haas">Johanna Haas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22180864-johanna-haas?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer668505869">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14930081562468438268">Whenever I read de Lint, I always feel like I'm sipping a coffee in an artist's cafe and eavesdropping on someone at the neighboring table telling fantastic stories. In Newford, there is always music in the air, always art around, always a friend handing you a hot cup of coffee or tea with a smile. , and always something strange flickering in and out from the corners of your vision. This collection of short stories is set in the imaginary city of Newford, telling us more about old characters and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14930081562468438268">Whenever I read de Lint, I always feel like I'm sipping a coffee in an artist's cafe and eavesdropping on someone at the neighboring table telling fantastic stories. In Newford, there is always music in the air, always art around, always a friend handing you a hot cup of coffee or tea with a smile. , and always something strange flickering in and out from the corners of your vision. This collection of short stories is set in the imaginary city of Newford, telling us more about old characters and introducing us to new ones - fully fleshed people I expect to run into around my town. It blends fairy mystery from a variety of cultures with a fully modern world. This is the first de Lint book I ever read - I selected it off the library shelf for its cover, years ago. Since then, I have been addicted to finding and reading all his work. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14930081562468438268">...more</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer563203855">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7575133868209264942">This is a collection of truly great stories. If you're familiar with other tales in this series, this is a great addition. If you're new to Newford it's a good introductory read even if it is #12. You can catch up later. These stories give leads to several of the characters from other books and introduce new ones. They explain the WildWood Webpage, and other story elements appearing elsewhere. Charles de Lint is a great storyteller and a luminous writer whose prose will haunt and carry you along</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7575133868209264942">This is a collection of truly great stories. If you're familiar with other tales in this series, this is a great addition. If you're new to Newford it's a good introductory read even if it is #12. You can catch up later. These stories give leads to several of the characters from other books and introduce new ones. They explain the WildWood Webpage, and other story elements appearing elsewhere. Charles de Lint is a great storyteller and a luminous writer whose prose will haunt and carry you along. His characters are generally like able but troubled, vivid and three dimensional. The supernatural elements merge several ancient traditions - Old World, Native American and Southwestern - with a modern world creating something unique. Enjoy. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7575133868209264942">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1854486-chere?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1854486-chere?shelf=faerie" class="actionLinkLite">faerie</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1854486-chere?shelf=short" class="actionLinkLite">short</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1854486-chere?shelf=stories" class="actionLinkLite">stories</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1854486-chere?shelf=urban" class="actionLinkLite">urban</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1854486-chere?shelf=collection" class="actionLinkLite">collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer274039672">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11629256107373582522">I'd only previously read Charles de Lint in anthologies, and while this is already his fourth Newford story collection, it's the perfect introduction for me to his magical city and its fascinating inhabitants. It's exactly my type of fantasy -- an urban setting that I can very easily relate to, but filled with wonders big and small. A regular cast of characters keep appearing in his tales, sometimes in center of the story and sometimes on the edges. While the stories can stand alone, reading the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11629256107373582522">I'd only previously read Charles de Lint in anthologies, and while this is already his fourth Newford story collection, it's the perfect introduction for me to his magical city and its fascinating inhabitants. It's exactly my type of fantasy -- an urban setting that I can very easily relate to, but filled with wonders big and small. A regular cast of characters keep appearing in his tales, sometimes in center of the story and sometimes on the edges. While the stories can stand alone, reading them all add to the richness of de Lint's fantasy world, and by the end of the book, I feel like I have been among old friends. I am looking forward to reading more of the author's works and catching up with them.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11629256107373582522">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9948658727293965044">I'm not a great reader of short stories, but I really like Charles de Lint and especially his Newford books. This collection of 17 stories and 1 novella is simply wonderful. Lots of magic, lots of music, some funny, some quite dark in tone, but they are beautifully written. Old friends like Jilly and Christy pop in and we find out a bit more about them.<br />My favourites in the set are "Ten For The Devil", (fancy meeting Robert Johnson here) and "Pixel Pixies". I just love the idea of a hob in a book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9948658727293965044">I'm not a great reader of short stories, but I really like Charles de Lint and especially his Newford books. This collection of 17 stories and 1 novella is simply wonderful. Lots of magic, lots of music, some funny, some quite dark in tone, but they are beautifully written. Old friends like Jilly and Christy pop in and we find out a bit more about them.<br />My favourites in the set are "Ten For The Devil", (fancy meeting Robert Johnson here) and "Pixel Pixies". I just love the idea of a hob in a bookshop, I could do with one for my study!<br />Off to the USA in August and hoping to pick up some more de Lint books while I'm there!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer37259199">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17075631039838399535">This is a great collection of short stories about Newford. Generally, I don't like short story collections, because I find it hard to switch context so quickly. But all the stories blend together beautifully, and because they're not limited by the need to stretch a story to a full book length, they're more mythic and somehow more substantial. It's a bit like reading a book of fables. Cesar and I frequently bemoan the lack of mythology in daily life, and the resulting spiritual poverty -- this co</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17075631039838399535">This is a great collection of short stories about Newford. Generally, I don't like short story collections, because I find it hard to switch context so quickly. But all the stories blend together beautifully, and because they're not limited by the need to stretch a story to a full book length, they're more mythic and somehow more substantial. It's a bit like reading a book of fables. Cesar and I frequently bemoan the lack of mythology in daily life, and the resulting spiritual poverty -- this collection makes a heroic dent in that lack.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer178122468">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17818046713656581646">This was a random find at a used book store. I was attracted by the beautiful cover art and couldn't be happier I picked it up. This was my first trip to Newford; undoubtedly there will be many more. This collection of short stories spoke candidly about the human condition in a way I had never experienced before. Life and death were at the center of every story, mixing science fiction with a keen sense of existentialism. De Lint did an excellent job here, and I hope his other works live up to th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17818046713656581646">This was a random find at a used book store. I was attracted by the beautiful cover art and couldn't be happier I picked it up. This was my first trip to Newford; undoubtedly there will be many more. This collection of short stories spoke candidly about the human condition in a way I had never experienced before. Life and death were at the center of every story, mixing science fiction with a keen sense of existentialism. De Lint did an excellent job here, and I hope his other works live up to this terrific read.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_192120663">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192120663" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4645312-tommy" class="left imgcol" title="Tommy /|\"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1360029711p2/4645312.jpg" alt="Tommy /|\" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/192120663?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 10, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4645312-tommy" class="user" title="Tommy /|\">Tommy /|\</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/186440.Tapping_the_Dream_Tree" title="Softcover 9780312868406" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer192120663">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16859631402906750920">A collection of short stories from DeLint's Newford world. I loved every single story in this book. DeLint's Newford stories remind me more of a mythological tale than a Fantasy story. Each character is given a chance to reveal as much of their background in each story (or as little) as seems necessary. The magic side of things - the fey, the Crow Girls (my favorites!), and a large multitude of others - is perfectly blended for both the believer and the skeptic. Absolutely loved it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5583116">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5075618607772877381">More short stories to read as interludes while I am still working on Anna Karenina. I have mixed feelings about de Lint. I enjoy his numerous books and stories, but there is something about them that makes me feel like they are too simple, or maybe it is the repetition of themes. Maybe it is the part of me that forgot that I like fairy stories and feels a little goofy about it. Maybe I feel trapped in Newford, but it's not a bad place to be... (May 06, 2004)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return

    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')

      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8185168.Charles_de_Lint">About Charles  de Lint</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/8185168.Charles_de_Lint"><img alt="8185168" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1400347166p2/8185168.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer47330934125951944">Charles de Lint is the much beloved author of more than seventy adult, young adult, and children's books. Renowned as one of the trailblazers of the modern fantasy genre, he is the recipient of the World Fantasy, Aurora, Sunburst, and White Pine awards, among others. Modern Library's Top 100 Books of the 20th Century poll, conducted by Random House and voted on by readers, put eight of de Lint's b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText47330934125951944">Charles de Lint is the much beloved author of more than seventy adult, young adult, and children's books. Renowned as one of the trailblazers of the modern fantasy genre, he is the recipient of the World Fantasy, Aurora, Sunburst, and White Pine awards, among others. Modern Library's Top 100 Books of the 20th Century poll, conducted by Random House and voted on by readers, put eight of de Lint's books among the top 100.<br />De Lint is a poet, folklorist, artist, songwriter and performer. He has written critical essays, music reviews, opinion columns and entries to encyclopedias, and he's been the main book reviewer for The Magazine of Fantasy &amp; Science Fiction since 1987. De Lint served as Writer-in-residence for two public libraries in Ottawa and has taught creative writing workshops for adults and children in Canada and the United States. He's been a judge for several prominent awards, including the Nebula, World Fantasy, Theodore Sturgeon and Bram Stoker.<br /><br />Born in the Netherlands in 1951, de Lint immigrated to Canada with his family as an infant. The family moved often during de Lint's childhood because of his father's job with an international surveying company, but by the time Charles was twelve—having lived in Western Canada, Turkey and Lebanon—they had settled in Lucerne, Quebec, not far from where he now resides in Ottawa, Ontario.<br /><br />In 1980, de Lint married the love of his life, MaryAnn Harris, who works closely with him as his first editor, business manager and creative partner. They share their love and home with a cheery little dog named Johnny Cash.<br /><br />Charles de Lint is best described as a romantic: a believer in compassion, hope and human potential. His skilled portrayal of character and settings has earned him a loyal readership and glowing praise from peers, reviewers and readers.<br /><br />Charles de Lint writes like a magician. He draws out the strange inside our own world, weaving stories that feel more real than we are when we read them. He is, simply put, the best. <br />—Holly Black (bestselling author)<br />Charles de Lint is the modern master of urban fantasy. Folktale, myth, fairy tale, dreams, urban legend—all of it adds up to pure magic in de Lint's vivid, original world. No one does it better. <br />—Alice Hoffman (bestselling author)<br /><br />To read de Lint is to fall under the spell of a master storyteller, to be reminded of the greatness of life, of the beauty and majesty lurking in shadows and empty doorways. <br />—Quill &amp; Quire<br /><br />His Newford books, which make up most of de Lint's body of work between 1993 and 2009, confirmed his reputation for bringing a vivid setting and repertory cast of characters to life on the page. Though not a consecutive series, the twenty-five standalone books set in (or connected to) Newford give readers a feeling of visiting a favourite city and seeing old friends.<br />More recently, his young adult Wildlings trilogy—Under My Skin, Over My Head, and Out of This World—came out from Penguin Canada and Triskell Press in 2012, 2013 and 2014. Under My Skin won 2013 Aurora Award. A novel for middle-grade readers, The Cats of Tanglewood Forest, published by Little Brown in 2013, won the Sunburst Award, earned starred reviews in both Publishers Weekly and Quill &amp; Quire, and was chosen by the New York Times Editors as one of the top six children's books for 2013. His most recent adult novel, The Mystery of Grace (2009), is a fascinating ghost story about love, passion and faith. It was a finalist for both the Sunburst and Evergreen awards.<br /><br />De Lint is presently writing a new adult novel. His storytelling skills also shine in his original songs. He and MaryAnn (also a musician) recently released companion CDs of their original songs, samples of which can be heard on de Lint's website. A multi-instrumentalist, his main instruments are guitar, harmonica and vocals, while MaryAnn's are mandolin, guitar, vocals and percussion.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="47330934125951944">...more</a>

    </div>

</a>
